Your voice, three dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last part of the science of assembled medicine and have finished it through its explanations and by its declarations. And it came to me in a vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is estranged from top to bottom, thus the science has perished and is decayed, and there remains nothing more of the fuels than the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved. And from this comes the error and the vanity, and the intentions are closed and the science is estranged.
It seems to me that I want to revive the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will assemble the forms of the iron instruments of cautery, and of the other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
And for the reason that no good masters of hands were found in our time, is the art of medicine extended. And it is necessary for the one who undertakes to thoroughly learn the science of anatomy, as Galien says, so that he knows the judgment of the members, and the forms and conjunctions and separations of them, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and brains and the number of them, and their movement and rest, and how they issue from there.
And for this reason said Hippocrates that the name is not much with the name, and with the work is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
We say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before, if he is not careful he will fall into error and harm people.
Therefore I have seen many of those who practice this science and abandon their sense and their experience.
For I saw a foolish doctor who cut into an abscess or swelling on a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of the neck. because so much blood flows out that the woman falls dead in his hands.
And I saw another mirror who treated a stone of a man's urine, and the stone was large; he took away with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if they had operated on him, he would have died.
And I saw another mirror who took in care the duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the breakage he had a wound;
and the mirror blamed ignorance for holding the breakage against the wound with very strong binding, and did not leave the wound any discharge, and thus he left it in this condition;
and he ordered that it should not be dislocated again;
and thus it remained until the leg was completely swollen and the foot, and came to ruin.
I am called to come to him, and I hurry to come to release his leg; and when I saw it dislocated thus it was in a country and he did not feel any pain.
But all the way the corruption was already confirmed on the limb, and I could not heal it;
and the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb so that the entire limb became almost entirely lost.
And he saw another doctor who burst open an abscess that was hidden, and then it became inflamed due to the evil of his lordship's malice.
For cancer, when it is pure melancholic humor, it does not seem that one should touch with iron unless the place is entirely clean so that one can remove all that is corrupted.
And for this, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: it is to know, whether there is danger in many dispositions;
and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Because it is necessary that you beware, so that foolish mirrors cannot speak badly of you.
If you take your arms in a cross, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way that for God's grace you come to health and be praised.
and leave the maladies to reveal the grievous sanity;
and lift your arms from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may be able to come from this world to the other of glory.
Galen says among some of his warnings: Do not take on the care of a bad disease, lest you be called foolish doctor.
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
The first chapters are about fire cauterization and medicinal cauterization, and these chapters are arranged from the head to the feet.
and about the forms of instruments, and the iron tools of cauterization, and all that is necessary in the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things;
and it is the ordered chapters and the forms of instruments.
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
and it is ordered according to the lower head just as feet, and the forms of instruments.
Here is the translation:
I say that the qualities of aid, and the harm, are the longest words and subtle science and the secret responses;
and from these they speak of the wisest men, and agree with them;
and I suffer little from their words, for I reduce the length.
I say that fire cautery universally aids every complexion where there is matter, before the two complexions: it is to know warm temperament without material, and dry temperament without material.
In warm and dry temperaments together with material, they devised none and said that cautery is a great aid; and the others said the opposite: that cautery is of no value for an illness that comes from chill and dryness. For the nature of fire is warm, and it should not be used to cure a warm illness through chill, nor through dryness;
and he said that those who say the opposite, that cautery makes great aid to warm and dry illnesses that come in the bodies of men. For when you examine the body of the man and its moisture according to the complexions of fire, you find the body cold.
And I agree with this statement. For I have found it true many times through experiment.
And in no way, one should not interfere with those who have experienced it, and who know through long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the events and the space of time;
of other complexions we have not so much fear, especially in cold and moist diseases. And all the mirrors assemble and agree with the cautery.
And know, son, that fire cautery is one of the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than medicine burning with ardor.
For fire is simple, and does not come except to the member that is cooked, and does not harm another member if it is not named.
The fiery remedies pass from one member to another by transmitting, and bring the diseased limb to a grievous sanitation; and sometimes kill the patient.
The fire, because of its height and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, if there is no excess.
And this I have found by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is established on the truth of things.
and for this I excuse myself from the length of the speech, because it does not please me that I withhold the secret which is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out the diseases of the body, as the philosopher said in demonstrating. for you receive in your thoughts.
And know, son, that they agree at the time when they should be done, the cauteries, and choose promptly.
And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the sudden injuries that occur are easily cured by the aid of cautery; and meanwhile the cauteries are for necessary pains and swift ones that cannot wait for the time when greater evil may come to the limb.
And do not think of anything, dear son, if you make the foolish mirror; for the illness that is healed by cautery has no relapse; and they say it thus;
and they say it thus; but it is not so as they think, because cauteries are not just a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors that are the cause of pain, and is more valuable than medicine for the speed of its effect, and for the virtue of its work and its dominion.
And it is possible that the disease comes at some time according to the temperament of the patient and the location of the illness and its power.
and are gathered in him the excesses through the acquisition of foods and similar things, if it is not cauterized in a place where there is little excess and moisture, just as cauterization is administered for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and that is true.
but they do not believe that cauterization is valuable after medicine, but their intentions are false, and it is cauterization the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of cures for any illness and they do not work, then we administer cauterization, and it is effective.
Then it appears clearly that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
The ancient ones said that cauteries of gold instrument are more effective than those of iron, and they did not say this because of the quality of gold and because of the height of its substance;
and they said that the eyes of the cautery do not make a bad wound, but this is not true because I have experienced it, and I have found that it is true in some men;
and cauteries of gold are worth more than those of iron, as they said loudly. And always when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is heated by the color of gold, and it is quickly cooled;
and if one heats it too much; they make at the fire; and thus there is enough of impediment.

of the pain of the teeth

The treatment of chancre by cautery
When a cancer appears at the beginning, and you want to stop it, if you cauterize with a cautery that resembles a circle, entirely around the tumor.
And always the wise men say that one should perform cauterization also at the middle of the channel of the sore;
and always it does not seem to me good, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already wanted to avoid it happening anytime;
and more rightfully it is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays healing or because of the superfluity that it does or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; and you hasten to amputate: then you cauterize around the area of small pricks, pricking; afterwards let it be so. For it hastens to worsen.
And if you want to pierce all around the cautery, then heat the cautery of copper, which is its form:
And put your hand in the middle of this illness called "adubelati" so that the cauteries have pierced the heart, and be such the cauteries that the patient feels relief in some manner that the course of the disease is alleviated.
Afterwards, treat until it is perfectly healthy.

of the dislocation of the shoulder
Know that the shoulder is not dislocated except in three ways:
because one of them is that it dislocates towards the back part at the joint; and the second is towards the front of the thigh; and sometimes it dislocates upwards, and that happens rarely;
and it does not dislocate backwards because of the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward because of the veins;
and often it dislocates downwards towards the joint, especially in those who have little flesh, because for them it happens suddenly;
For those who have enough flesh, it pierces at points, and re-enters at points.
And by chance it happens to some men that they receive a blow or fracture, and the shoulder is inflamed with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
It is necessary therefore that you test them, as long as you are certain of them; and then begin the treatment.
And it is known that dislocations occur when it falls towards the joint, and makes a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them a manifest diversity; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the joint, touching the head of the shoulder, as if it were a bone; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move with any movements;
and thus, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the joint;
and this manner of dislocation is not forcing to recall, when it is new, or if the veins are diseased.
And the method is that the ministers lift the hand of the patient upwards high, then put their fingers underneath the shoulder blade, and lift the joint with force upwards to its place; and the ministers lift the hand, and stretch it upwards, then put it underneath; if it will come quickly.
And if it does not come as we have said in many days afterwards, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in warm water; and the minister applies soothing and calming remedies, such as a decoction of lettuce and fenugreek and melilot in warm water, and it is soothed;
then the patient is laid on their back, and a strip of linen cloth, not too soft nor too hard, is placed underneath the shoulder blade, then the minister places their heel on the strip, and lifts the head of the shoulder strongly, and draws the hand of the patient;
and another minister touches the head of the patient, so that he does not move downwards; that shoulder returns now entirely, and if you see whether it is reset according to this method:
and it is that you make the bone which is more massive than the patient's; and be straight towards the ribcage, and push the shoulder down to the bone of the patient's, and lift the bone high up, so that the patient's arm hangs in the air; and another minister draws the patient's hand downwards towards the belly. And if the patient is too lightweight, then weigh him down with something heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
And it is reset in another way:
and it is as if one fixes a long pole on the ground, so that the head is also straight like a pestle, and neither too large nor too slender; then it should be placed under the patient, but so that it has soft drapery above, and the patient is standing straight from the long pole of the beam;
Then let his hand be extended downward from the other part in a straight line, and the joint will quickly return to its place.
and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then make this treatment: Take a stick of two feet in length and four fingers in width, which has the top end rounded to enter obliquely into the hollow of the joint, according to this form:
then place the top end of the stick wrapped in cloths, so that the stick does not touch the patient, then put it under the joint of the patient;
and extend the arm along the length of the stick, and place the shoulder on the stick, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on a small stool of a chair, and let the hand be extended downward, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint returns to its place now
And when it is in, whatever way it may be, it is necessary that you place under the seat a layer of even linen, then put on top the plaster made from powder of soft millet, with incense and album of egg white, across the entire shoulder and around, then hold under the seat firmly, and turn the ligature on the plaster, and bind the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
And it is necessary to nourish a little, as long as the limb is comforted, for it will heal more quickly;
and then nourish more afterwards 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is strengthened and not softened, it is healed.
And if the joint is out of place due to moisture or another cause, then it is necessary that you administer cauterizations at three points, as it is described before in the chapter on cauterizations.
And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is affected or stretched out or softened. and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
The dislocation that is towards the chest, and the breasts, or behind, if made by impulse, and stretching of hands, and it needs another treatment.
and heal as long as he is healthy.
And after the healing comes numbness to the limb, and later on it has difficulty in movement, if the patient bathes many times, so that this numbness is alleviated, and it returns to its original nature.
of the dislocation where it hurts
Know that the joint of the hip is dislocated to points, and at points returns;
and it is dislocated in all parts, and meanwhile before and behind, and the dislocation is not fully restored, for one sees well and feels well; and dislocates according to each shape. And when you join the injured limb with the healthy one, then it can be seen openly. For the joint is crooked, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
And it is necessary that you reset it thus so that abscesses do not gather there, for if abscesses gather there, it would be grievous to reset;
and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is behind; if it is worse than the other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death comes.
And the restoration is, when it is such that one can reset it, that you extend your hand to your two hands; and his arms should be expansive, and the hands soft in the mirror according to the count of the interior, above and below, and bent the jointure at his fingers assembled, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.

and if you see that the joint does not fix well, then reapply the poultice and the ligament, and let it go thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then disentangle it.

and if you see that, put a warm poultice of soft butter on it, and hold it in place;
if it returns to its proper position.
the dislocation of the hand
The joint of the hand dislocates, and the return is easy, more so than the other joints. However, it is necessary to return it to its place quickly, in the same way that it was dislocated, so that the limbs are not swollen, or an abscess does not form there.
And the way to return it is that you put the injured hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of the hand, and the doctor puts them in alignment, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and presses until it returns.
However, you go ahead, it is necessary to examine if it is well in its place; then put the patient's hand on a table at extension and at flexion. And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then place the patient's hand on the table, and the doctor places his hand on the appearance of the joint.
If it returns now, that is good. If not, then strain the emplasters calming abscesses and let them sense re-commence.
And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it in its place after several days, the twisted joint remains.
and do not annoy the patient further unless the hand is numb, and cannot strain anything at all: then know that the nerves are injured, or the arteries;
if there is no other remedy except to strain by cauterization in this case, and by chance it will not be worth anything else.
And when the hand is on the spot, put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then hold it and leave it thus for a while, then remove it and leave it so.
And if it cannot move well, and there is no grinding, then soak the swollen area in warm water, and rub it so that it becomes healthy.
of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Never are the fingers of the hand dislocated to any part, never to the back of the palm or to the belly;

and do everything thus, when it is dislocated from another part.
for the dislocation of the spine of the back
When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, where there are multiple dislocations, if there is no point of healing, because death hastens the patient.

Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come to be dislocated solely, not so like the other joints;

And the signs of the one who is near death, if it is that these accidents are contrary to those beforehand.

of the dislocation of the knee
The knee is dislocated in three ways: it is to know, inward and forward, and backward;
and do not dislocate at all in front.
And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg to their thigh, and if it does not adhere to their thigh, know that it is dislocated;
and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg as they can, and place your back against their face, and put their foot on your feet;
Then take your knee in your palms, and draw it back between your thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee in a circular shape. and another minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that he has well aligned his leg with his hip lightly.

of the dislocation of the ankle
The ankles are sometimes sprained and sometimes completely dislocated, and inwardly and outwardly.

if it returns, that's good;

of wound and dislocation together
When a wound comes with a dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:
if you are not presumptuous in the cure, be wise in the art and you have not used it for a long time, and be piteous and merciful and slow, not harsh;
and apply gentle remedies at the beginning of hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the hot abscesses will not return;
and when the limb is out of place, if you administer soothing remedies to the inflamed abscess, and treat the wound, as it is fitting, with dry dressings.
and also with a fracture or breakage, and less severe dislocations, if you reduce the swelling, and do what we have said about simple illnesses.
and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, for it will be of no value to you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and your body.
